      'net/mlx5e RX, Fix generating s...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-40350',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 14:15:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'net/mlx5e RX, Fix generating skb from non-linear xdp_buff for striding RQ\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'XDP programs can change the layout of an xdp_buff through\r\n' +
      'bpf_xdp_adjust_tail() and bpf_xdp_adjust_head(). Therefore, the driver\r\n' +
      'cannot assume the size of the linear data area nor fragments. Fix the\r\n' +
      'bug in mlx5 by generating skb according to xdp_buff after XDP programs\r\n' +
      'run.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Currently, when handling multi-buf XDP, the mlx5 driver assumes the\r\n' +
      'layout of an xdp_buff to be unchanged. That is, the linear data area\r\n' +
      'continues to be empty and fragments remain the same. This may cause\r\n' +
      'the driver to generate erroneous skb or triggering a kernel\r\n' +
      'warning. When an XDP program added linear data through\r\n' +
      'bpf_xdp_adjust_head(), the linear data will be ignored as\r\n' +
      'mlx5e_build_linear_skb() builds an skb without linear data and then\r\n' +
      'pull data from fragments to fill the linear data area. When an XDP\r\n' +
      'program has shrunk the non-linear data through bpf_xdp_adjust_tail(),\r\n' +
      'the delta passed to __pskb_pull_tail() may exceed the actual nonlinear\r\n' +
      'data size and trigger the BUG_ON in it.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'To fix the issue, first record the original number of fragments. If the\r\n' +
      'number of fragments changes after the XDP program runs, rewind the end\r\n' +
      'fragment pointer by the difference and recalculate the truesize. Then,\r\n' +
      'build the skb with the linear data area matching the xdp_buff. Finally,\r\n' +
      'only pull data in if there is non-linear data and fill the linear part\r\n' +
      'up to 256 bytes. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>',

      '    $ceph fs authorize fsname1 client.usr / r\r\n' +
      "3. Authorize read and write permission to the same user 'client.usr' on fs 'fsname2'\r\n" +
      '    $ceph fs authorize fsname2 client.usr / rw\r\n' +
      '4. Update the keyring\r\n' +
      '    $ceph auth get client.usr >> ./keyring\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      "With above permssions for the user 'client.usr', following is the\r\n" +
      'expectation.\r\n' +
      "  a. The 'client.usr' should be able to only read the contents\r\n" +
      "     and not allowed to create or delete files on file system 'fsname1'.\r\n" +
      "  b. The 'client.usr' should be able to read/write on file system 'fsname2'.\r\n" +

      "But, with this bug, the 'client.usr' is allowed to read/write on file\r\n" +
      "system 'fsname1'. See below.\r\n" +

      '     $sudo bin/mount.ceph usr@.fsname1=/ /kmnt_fsname1_usr/\r\n' +

      '   should fail but passes with this bug.\r\n' +
      '     $touch /kmnt_fsname1_usr/file1\r\n' +

      'and tests added by looking into the tracker mentioned below.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'v2 Fix a possible null dereference in doutc\r\n' +
      "v3 Don't store fsname from mdsmap, validate against\r\n" +
      "    ceph_mount_options's fsname and use it\r\n" +
      'v4 Code refactor, better warning message and\r\n' +

    content: '![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'netpoll Fix deadlock in memory allocation under spinlock\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Fix a AA deadlock in refill_skbs() where memory allocation while holding\r\n' +
      'skb_pool->lock can trigger a recursive lock acquisition attempt.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The deadlock scenario occurs when the system is under severe memory\r\n' +
      'pressure\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '1. refill_skbs() acquires skb_pool->lock (spinlock)\r\n' +
      '2. alloc_skb() is called while holding the lock\r\n' +
      '3. Memory allocator fails and calls slab_out_of_memory()\r\n' +
      '4. This triggers printk() for the OOM warning\r\n' +
      '5. The console output path calls netpoll_send_udp()\r\n' +
      '6. netpoll_send_udp() attempts to acquire the same skb_pool->lock\r\n' +
      '7. Deadlock the lock is already held by the same CPU\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Call stack\r\n' +
      '  refill_skbs()\r\n' +
      '    spin_lock_irqsave(skb_pool->lock)    - lock acquired\r\n' +
      '    __alloc_skb()\r\n' +
      '      kmem_cache_alloc_node_noprof()\r\n' +
      '        slab_out_of_memory()\r\n' +
      '          printk()\r\n' +
      '            console_flush_all()\r\n' +
      '              netpoll_send_udp()\r\n' +
      '                skb_dequeue()\r\n' +
      '                  spin_lock_irqsave(skb_pool->lock)     - deadlock attempt\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This bug was exposed by commit 248f6571fd4c51 ("netpoll Optimize skb\r\n' +
      'refilling on critical path") which removed refill_skbs() from the\r\n' +
      'critical path (where nested printk was being deferred), letting nested\r\n' +
      'printk being called from inside refill_skbs()\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Refactor refill_skbs() to never allocate memory while holding\r\n' +
      'the spinlock.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Another possible solution to fix this problem is protecting the\r\n' +
      'refill_skbs() from nested printks, basically calling\r\n' +
      'printk_deferred_{enter,exit}() in refill_skbs(), then, any nested\r\n' +
      'pr_warn() would be deferred.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'I prefer this approach, given I _think_ it might be a good idea to move\r\n' +
      'the alloc_skb() from GFP_ATOMIC to GFP_KERNEL in the future, so, having\r\n' +
      'the alloc_skb() outside of the lock will be necessary step.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'There is a possible TOCTOU issue when checking for the pool length, and\r\n' +
      'queueing the new allocated skb, but, this is not an issue, given that\r\n' +
      'an extra SKB in the pool is harmless and it will be eventually used. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>',

    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-68175',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 14:15:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'media nxp imx8-isi Fix streaming cleanup on release\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The current implementation unconditionally calls\r\n' +
      'mxc_isi_video_cleanup_streaming() in mxc_isi_video_release(). This can\r\n' +
      'lead to situations where any release call (like from a simple\r\n' +
      '"v4l2-ctl -l") may release a currently streaming queue when called on\r\n' +
      'such a device.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This is reproducible on an i.MX8MP board by streaming from an ISI\r\n' +
      'capture device using gstreamer\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '\tgst-launch-1.0 -v v4l2src device=/dev/videoX ! \\\r\n' +
      '\t    video/x-raw,format=GRAY8,width=1280,height=800,framerate=1/120 ! \\\r\n' +
      '\t    fakesink\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      'As reported by Luiz Capitulino enabling HVO on s390 leads to reproducible\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      'Even if it looks like the empty flush_tlb_all() implementation on s390 is\r\n' +
      'the problem, it is actually a different problem on s390 it is not allowed\r\n' +
      'to replace an active/valid page table entry with another valid page table\r\n' +
      'entry without the detour over an invalid entry. A direct replacement may\r\n' +
      'lead to random crashes and/or data corruption.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'In order to invalidate an entry special instructions have to be used\r\n' +
      '(e.g. ipte or idte). Alternatively there are also special instructions\r\n' +
      'available which allow to replace a valid entry with a different valid\r\n' +
      'entry (e.g. crdte or cspg).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Given that the HVO code currently does not provide the hooks to allow for\r\n' +
      'an implementation which is compliant with the s390 architecture\r\n' +
      'requirements, disable ARCH_WANT_OPTIMIZE_HUGETLB_VMEMMAP again, which is\r\n' +
      'basically a revert of the original patch which enabled it. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>',

  {
    title: 'CVE-2025-68194 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'media imon make send_packet()...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-68194',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 14:15:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'media imon make send_packet() more robust\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'syzbot is reporting that imon has three problems which result in\r\n' +
      'hung tasks due to forever holding device lock [1].\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'First problem is that when usb_rx_callback_intf0() once got -EPROTO error\r\n' +
      'after ictx->dev_present_intf0 became true, usb_rx_callback_intf0()\r\n' +
      'resubmits urb after printk(), and resubmitted urb causes\r\n' +
      'usb_rx_callback_intf0() to again get -EPROTO error. This results in\r\n' +
      'printk() flooding (RCU stalls).\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Alan Stern commented [2] that\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      "  In theory it's okay to resubmit _if_ the driver has a robust\r\n" +
      '  error-recovery scheme (such as giving up after some fixed limit on the\r\n' +
      '  number of errors or after some fixed time has elapsed, perhaps with a\r\n' +
      "  time delay to prevent a flood of errors).  Most drivers don't bother to\r\n" +
      '  do this they simply give up right away.  This makes them more\r\n' +
      '  vulnerable to short-term noise interference during USB transfers, but in\r\n' +
      "  reality such interference is quite rare.  There's nothing really wrong\r\n" +
      '  with giving up right away.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'but imon has a poor error-recovery scheme which just retries forever\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +

      "  time delay to prevent a flood of errors).  Most drivers don't bother to\r\n" +

      '  vulnerable to short-term noise interference during USB transfers, but in\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +

      '        }\r\n' +

      'table ip nat {\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +
      '    def foo(i)\r\n' +
      '      if i == 1\r\n' +
      '        use 128 bytes of stack\r\n' +

      'while queued_st->allocated_stack is much smaller.\r\n' +

      '    prev_st = find_prev_entry(env, ...)\r\n' +
      '    queued_st = push_stack(...)\r\n' +
      '    widen_imprecise_scalars(env, prev_st, queued_st)\r\n' +

      'depth as queued_st. E.g. in the following case\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '    def main()\r\n' +
      '      for i in 1..2\r\n' +
      '        foo(i)        // same callsite, differnt param\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '    def foo(i)\r\n' +
      '      if i == 1\r\n' +
      '        use 128 bytes of stack\r\n' +
      '      iterator based loop\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      "Here, for a second 'foo' call prev_st->allocated_stack is 128,\r\n" +
      'while queued_st->allocated_stack is much smaller.\r\n' +
      'widen_imprecise_scalars() needs to take this into account and avoid\r\n' +

      'by an EQ interrupt and call a completion function intended only for user\r\n' +
      'CQs, causing a null pointer exception.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Some areas in the driver have prevented this issue with one-off fixes\r\n' +
      'but did not address the root cause.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This patch fixes the described issue by adding defaults to the create CQ\r\n' +
      'flow. It adds a default dummy completion function to protect against\r\n' +
      'null pointer exceptions, and it sets an invalid command sequence number\r\n' +
      'by default in kernel CQs to prevent the FW from sending an interrupt to\r\n' +
      'the CQ until it is armed. User CQs are responsible for their own\r\n' +
      'initialization values.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +

      '\r\n' +

      '        *area = 0\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '        /* Enable KSM. */\r\n' +
      '        madvise(area, size, MADV_MERGEABLE)\r\n' +
      '        pause()\r\n' +
      '        return 0\r\n' +
      '}\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '$ ./ksm-sparse  \r\n' +

    title: 'CVE-2025-68214 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'timers Fix NULL function point...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-68214',
    pubDate: 'Tue, 16 Dec 2025 14:15:00 GMT',
    content: '![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'timers Fix NULL function pointer race in timer_shutdown_sync()\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'There is a race condition between timer_shutdown_sync() and timer\r\n' +
      'expiration that can lead to hitting a WARN_ON in expire_timers().\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The issue occurs when timer_shutdown_sync() clears the timer function\r\n' +
      'to NULL while the timer is still running on another CPU. The race\r\n' +
      'scenario looks like this\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'CPU0\t\t\t\t\tCPU1\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tSOFTIRQ>\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\texpire_timers()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tbase->running_timer = timer\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tunlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t[call_timer_fn enter]\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tmod_timer()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t...\r\n' +
      'timer_shutdown_sync()\r\n' +
      'lock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '// For now, will not detach the timer but only clear its function to NULL\r\n' +
      'if (base->running_timer != timer)\r\n' +
      '\tret = detach_if_pending(timer, base, true)\r\n' +
      'if (shutdown)\r\n' +
      '\ttimer->function = NULL\r\n' +
      'unlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t[call_timer_fn exit]\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tbase->running_timer = NULL\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tunlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t...\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t// Now timer is pending while its function set to NULL.\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t// next timer trigger\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tSOFTIRQ>\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\texpire_timers()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tWARN_ON_ONCE(!fn) // hit\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t...\r\n' +
      'lock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '// Now timer will detach\r\n' +
      'if (base->running_timer != timer)\r\n' +
      '\tret = detach_if_pending(timer, base, true)\r\n' +
      'if (shutdown)\r\n' +
      '\ttimer->function = NULL\r\n' +
      'unlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The problem is that timer_shutdown_sync() clears the timer function\r\n' +
      'regardless of whether the timer is currently running. This can leave a\r\n' +
      'pending timer with a NULL function pointer, which triggers the\r\n' +
      'WARN_ON_ONCE(!fn) check in expire_timers().\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Fix this by only clearing the timer function when actually detaching the\r\n' +
      'timer. If the timer is running, leave the function pointer intact, which is\r\n' +
      'safe because the timer will be properly detached when it finishes running. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>',
    contentSnippet: '![CDATA[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'timers Fix NULL function pointer race in timer_shutdown_sync()\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'There is a race condition between timer_shutdown_sync() and timer\r\n' +
      'expiration that can lead to hitting a WARN_ON in expire_timers().\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The issue occurs when timer_shutdown_sync() clears the timer function\r\n' +
      'to NULL while the timer is still running on another CPU. The race\r\n' +
      'scenario looks like this\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'CPU0\t\t\t\t\tCPU1\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tSOFTIRQ>\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\texpire_timers()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tbase->running_timer = timer\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tunlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t[call_timer_fn enter]\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tmod_timer()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t...\r\n' +
      'timer_shutdown_sync()\r\n' +
      'lock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '// For now, will not detach the timer but only clear its function to NULL\r\n' +
      'if (base->running_timer != timer)\r\n' +
      '\tret = detach_if_pending(timer, base, true)\r\n' +
      'if (shutdown)\r\n' +
      '\ttimer->function = NULL\r\n' +
      'unlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t[call_timer_fn exit]\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tbase->running_timer = NULL\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tunlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t...\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t// Now timer is pending while its function set to NULL.\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t// next timer trigger\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tSOFTIRQ>\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\texpire_timers()\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\tWARN_ON_ONCE(!fn) // hit\r\n' +
      '\t\t\t\t\t...\r\n' +
      'lock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '// Now timer will detach\r\n' +
      'if (base->running_timer != timer)\r\n' +
      '\tret = detach_if_pending(timer, base, true)\r\n' +
      'if (shutdown)\r\n' +
      '\ttimer->function = NULL\r\n' +
      'unlock_timer_base()\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The problem is that timer_shutdown_sync() clears the timer function\r\n' +
      'regardless of whether the timer is currently running. This can leave a\r\n' +
      'pending timer with a NULL function pointer, which triggers the\r\n' +
      'WARN_ON_ONCE(!fn) check in expire_timers().\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Fix this by only clearing the timer function when actually detaching the\r\n' +
      'timer. If the timer is running, leave the function pointer intact, which is\r\n' +
      'safe because the timer will be properly detached when it finishes running. | Severity UNKNOWN  ]]>',
    guid: 'CVE-2025-68214',
    isoDate: '2025-12-16T14:15:00.000Z'
